It was kind of like Comic-Con, but all Disney, all the time, and with a lot more talk about stock options. We here at /Film covered the biggest of the big news yesterday, but there were still plenty of odds and ends left to round-up.</p>\n<p>So gather round, children, and allow me to tell you the tale of the future Disney has in store for all of us. As a wise man once said, we are all interested in the future, for that is where you and I are going to spend the rest of our lives.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-649848\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Three-Men-and-a-Baby-remake.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-630830\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Three-Men-and-a-Baby-remake-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Three Men and a Baby remake\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Three-Men-and-a-Baby-remake.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Three-Men-and-a-Baby-remake-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Three Men and a Baby</strong></h2>\n<p><strong><em>Three Men and a</em> <em>Baby</em></strong>, a 1987 film that was a remake of the French film <em>Trois hommes et un couffin</em>, is getting a remake from the folks at Disney. Disney describes it as a &#8220;modern take on the hilarious &#8217;80s comedy,&#8221; and adds that it will star <strong>Zac Efron</strong>. Disney doesn&#8217;t specify who he&#8217;s playing, so I&#8217;m just going to go ahead and assume he&#8217;s playing the baby. In the &#8217;87 film, three bachelor roommates accidentally get stuck with a baby, and hilarity ensues. Also, there&#8217;s a subplot about drug smuggling for some reason. Anyway, the new <em>Three Men and a Baby</em> is headed to Disney+ in<strong> 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-28-1.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649852\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-28-1-700x394.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-28-1-700x394.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-28-1-360x203.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-28-1-768x432.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Real-Life Sports Stories </strong></h2>\n<p>This isn&#8217;t one project, it&#8217;s three. Disney will be making three films inspired by the true stories of <strong>Chris Paul</strong>, a basketball player for the Phoenix Suns; <span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\"><strong>Giannis Antetokounmpo</strong>, a basketball player for the </span>Milwaukee Bucks; and <strong>Keanon Lowe</strong>, the &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.kgw.com/article/news/local/parkrose-hero-keanon-lowe-disney-movie-portland/283-6c8b7ce5-73d6-4352-9440-af6668ba04b2\">Oregon football star</a> who became a hero off the field when he disarmed a student who brought a gun to Parkrose High School.&#8221; Here&#8217;s the part where I tell you I really don&#8217;t follow sports, at all, so I&#8217;ve never heard of any of these gentlemen before. But I&#8217;m sure there are plenty of people who are interested in seeing these titles whenever they arrive on Disney+.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649856\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv-700x1034.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"1034\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv-700x1034.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv-339x500.jpeg 339w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv-768x1134.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6iUHtW4AM9ncv.jpeg 1088w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Flora and Ulysses</strong></h2>\n<p>How&#8217;s this for a synopsis: in <strong><em>Flora and Ulysses</em></strong>, &#8220;<span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">A cynical young comic book fan and her superpowered squirrel sidekick team up.&#8221; The upcoming Disney+ film (it drops on February 19) is based on the book by writer Kate DiCamillo and illustrator K.G. Campbell, and comes from director <strong>Lena Khan</strong>. And hey, Alyson <strong>Hannigan</strong> is in the movie! That&#8217;s something!</span></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649857\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889-700x271.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"271\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889-700x271.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889-360x140.png 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889-768x298.png 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cheaper-by-the-dozen-556d84cb04889.png 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Cheaper by the Dozen</strong></h2>\n<p>The <strong><em>Cheaper by the Dozen</em></strong> series is getting a reimagining from <em>Blackish</em> producer <strong>Kenya Barris</strong>. The film &#8220;<span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">centers on a blended family of 12, navigating a hectic home life and their family business,&#8221; and <strong>Gabrielle Union</strong> is set to star. The original <em>Cheaper by the Dozen</em> starred Clifton Webb and opened in 1950. It was remade with Steven Martin in 2003. This latest version arrives in 2022 on Disney+.</span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/diaryofawimpykid-longhaul-familyroadtrip.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-400659\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/diaryofawimpykid-longhaul-familyroadtrip-700x306.jpg\" alt=\"Diary of a Wimpy Kid The Long Haul Trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"306\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/diaryofawimpykid-longhaul-familyroadtrip-700x306.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/diaryofawimpykid-longhaul-familyroadtrip-360x157.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/diaryofawimpykid-longhaul-familyroadtrip.jpg 803w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Diary of a Wimpy Kid</strong></h2>\n<p>Remember the live-action <strong><em>Diary of a Wimpy Kid</em></strong> movies? Well, they&#8217;re moving to Disney+&#8230;in animated form. Rather than keep the live-action series going, Disney is instead making an all-new animated <em>Wimpy Kid</em> film for 2021 on, you guessed it, Disney+. The films are based on the book series that take the form of &#8220;journals of the main character, Greg Heffley. Befitting a teen&#8217;s diary, the books are filled with simple drawings of Greg&#8217;s daily adventures.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649860\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ice-age-adventures.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">The Ice Age Adventures of Buck Wild</span></strong></h2>\n<p>Quick, without looking it up – how many <em><strong>Ice Ag</strong>e</em> movies are there? If you guessed 10,000, you are correct. And here is another one – <strong><em>The Ice Age Adventures of Buck Wild</em></strong>. The film features &#8220;<span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">prankster possum brothers Crash and Eddie, and swashbuckling weasel Buck.&#8221; Buck is voiced by <strong>Simon Pegg</strong>. But I&#8217;m sure you already knew that, reader, because <em>Ice Age</em> is an important series that we all know and love and cherish. Look for this thing in 2022 on Disney+. At this point, I&#8217;m pretty sure the <em>Ice Age</em> franchise has lasted longer than the actual Ice Age (please don&#8217;t look this up to correct me). </span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649862\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/night-at-the-museum-animated.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Night at the Museum </strong></h2>\n<p>Another live-action series getting an animated reboot: <strong><em>Night at the Museum</em></strong>. <strong>Shawn Levy</strong>, who helmed the live-action series, is producing. There is next to no info about this, but the films involve <strong>Ben Stiller</strong> as a security guard who is haunted by the ghosts of history! Spooky! Disney+ will invite you into the museum in 2021.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-dwayne-johnson-emily-blunt.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-616501\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-dwayne-johnson-emily-blunt-700x293.jpg\" alt=\"ball and chain\" width=\"700\" height=\"293\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-dwayne-johnson-emily-blunt-700x293.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-dwayne-johnson-emily-blunt-360x151.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-dwayne-johnson-emily-blunt-768x322.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Jungle Cruise</strong></h2>\n<p><strong><em>Jungle Cruise</em></strong>, the first Disney movie from <em>Orphan</em> and <em>The Shallows</em> director <strong>Jaume Collet-Serra</strong>, was supposed to open in October of 2019. Then it got moved to July 24, 2020 – only to be pushed again due to the coronavirus pandemic. It&#8217;s now set to open on July 21, 2021. This isn&#8217;t news, we knew this already, but Disney still felt the need to remind us. Or perhaps they wanted to drive home the fact that the film is sticking with its theatrical plan and not headed to Disney+. The movie, based on the theme park attraction, stars <strong>Dwayne Johnson</strong>, <strong>Emily Blunt</strong>, <strong>Édgar Ramírez</strong>, <strong>Jack Whitehall</strong>, <strong>Jesse Plemons</strong>, and <strong>Paul Giamatti</strong>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-lion-king-4-e1568669570846.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-569025\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-lion-king-4-e1568669570846-700x347.jpg\" alt=\"the lion king blu-ray and digital release\" width=\"700\" height=\"347\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-lion-king-4-e1568669570846-700x347.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-lion-king-4-e1568669570846-360x178.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-lion-king-4-e1568669570846-768x380.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Lion King Prequel</strong></h2>\n<p>As previously <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-lion-king-live-action-sequel-barry-jenkins-to-direct/\">reported</a>, <strong>Barry Jenkins</strong> is making a follow-up to the &#8220;live-action&#8221; remake of <strong><em>The Lion King</em></strong>. Initially, it was rumored to be a sequel, but since then we&#8217;ve learned it&#8217;s a prequel. And other reports indicate the prequel follows Mufasa in his early days. Beyond that, well, we don&#8217;t know much. But <strong>Hans Zimmer</strong>, <strong>Pharrell Williams,</strong> and Jenkins&#8217; go-to composer <strong>Nicholas Britell</strong> are all working on the music. So there&#8217;s that.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649864\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW-700x700.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"700\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW-700x700.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW-360x360.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW-768x768.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jVzsXcAQgZrW.jpeg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>The Little Mermaid</strong></h2>\n<p>Speaking of live-action remakes, we already knew that a live-action <strong><em>Little Mermaid</em></strong> was on the way. And we already knew who was starring in it. But Disney went ahead and made it official: <strong>Halle Bailey</strong> is Ariel, <strong>Daveed Diggs</strong> is Sebastian, <strong>Javier Bardem</strong> is King Triton, <strong>Jacob Tremblay</strong> is Flounder, <strong>Melissa McCarthy</strong> is Ursula, <strong>Jonah Hauer-King</strong> is Prince Eric, and <strong>Awkwafina</strong> is Scuttle. There you have it. <strong>Rob Marshall</strong> is directing, and the film will feature music from the original movie, and new music by <strong>Alen Menken</strong> and <strong>Lin-Manuel Mirand</strong>a. Production on the film was delayed due to the pandemic, but during the presentation yesterday,  CEO Bob Chapek said all postponed films had started shooting again.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649865\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9-700x350.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"350\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9-700x350.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9-360x180.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9-768x384.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6jbUHXYAIWDr9.jpeg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">Chip N&#8217; Dale: Rescue Rangers</span></strong></h2>\n<p>Of all the announcements yesterday, I&#8217;ll confess this was the one I got the biggest kick out of. Not because I particularly care about characters Chip and Dale, but because the idea of rebooting them with the voices of <strong>John Mulaney</strong> and <strong>Andy Samberg</strong> is very, very funny. The new <strong><em>Chip N&#8217; Dale: Rescue Rangers</em> </strong>will be a live-action-animated hybrid film directed by <strong>Akiva Schaffe</strong>r. It&#8217;s headed to Disney+.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649867\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056-700x394.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056-700x394.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056-360x203.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056-768x432.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pinocchiothumb-1607652553056.jpg 1280w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Pinocchio</strong></h2>\n<p>We got our first look, of sorts, at<strong> Robert Zemeckis</strong>&#8216; live-action <strong><em>Pinocchio</em></strong>. It&#8217;s been rumored for a while now that the film would reunite Zemeckis and <strong>Tom Hanks</strong>, and sure enough, it looks like it is. Hanks is playing Gepetto. And the film is headed to Disney+. I&#8217;m sure someone, somewhere, is excited about this, but based on the last few years of Zemeckis&#8217; career, I&#8217;m not.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">One of Disney’s all-time classics is coming to <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/DisneyPlus?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#DisneyPlus</a> with the new live-action retelling of Pinocchio, starring Tom Hanks and directed by Robert Zemeckis. ? <a href=\"https://t.co/44bHbFRhMe\">pic.twitter.com/44bHbFRhMe</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Walt Disney Studios (@DisneyStudios) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DisneyStudios/status/1337186518004355072?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 11, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-2.39.51-PM.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649868\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-2.39.51-PM-700x345.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"345\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-2.39.51-PM-700x345.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-2.39.51-PM-360x177.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-2.39.51-PM-768x379.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Peter Pan &#38; Wendy</strong></h2>\n<p>David Lowery&#8217;s <em>Pete&#8217;s Dragon</em> was the only film in the recent &#8220;live-action remake&#8221; trend that Disney is all-in on that I enjoyed, so I am marginally excited for <strong><em>Peter Pan and Wendy</em></strong>, another live-action remake headed to Disney+. Disney swears! And they&#8217;re bringing it Disney+! And <strong>Amy Adams</strong> is back! There&#8217;s still no release date, though. So you&#8217;ll just have to keep waiting. In the original film (which, oddly enough, currently <em>isn&#8217;t</em> on Disney+), &#8220;In the fairy-tale land of Andalasia, pretty young Giselle frolics with her woodland pals, and falls in love with the handsome Prince Edward, but when Giselle arrives at the castle to marry her Prince Charming, his evil stepmother sends the princess-to-be to a place where there are `no happy ever afters&#8217;: New York City. Cynical divorce lawyer Robert comes to her rescue, but can Giselle find her way back to her true love?&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-524053\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"sister act 3 update\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/sister-act-3-update.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Sister Act 3</strong></h2>\n<p>Back in 2018, I wrote up a <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/sister-act-3/\">story</a> about <strong><em>Sister Act 3</em></strong> being in development at Disney+. At the time, <strong>Whoopi Goldberg,</strong> star of the original two films, wasn&#8217;t involved. But now Disney+ says she is, and that the film is being produced by Tyler Perry, and that it&#8217;s headed to Disney+. In the original, Goldberg played a lounge singer who witnesses a murder and goes into hiding in a convent. And then she teaches all the nuns to sing and have fun. It&#8217;s a cute, harmless movie.<span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">.</span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6oaaXU0AAbViI.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649870\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6oaaXU0AAbViI-700x398.jpeg\" alt=\"Iwájú\" width=\"700\" height=\"398\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6oaaXU0AAbViI-700x398.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6oaaXU0AAbViI-360x205.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Eo6oaaXU0AAbViI-768x437.jpeg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">Iwájú</span></strong></h2>\n<p>Finally, here&#8217;s <strong><em>Iwájú</em></strong>. Disney Animation teamed with <span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-1qd0xha r-ad9z0x r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">Pan-African entertainment company Kugali to create an &#8220;all-new, science fiction series coming to Disney+ in 2022.&#8221; Per Deadline, the series will have &#8220;deep themes of class, innocence and challenging the status quo,&#8221; and Walt Disney Animation Studios’ chief creative officer Jennifer Lee added that the series will also &#8220;bring African stories created by African artist to the world, highlighting the diversity of cultures, histories and voices across the continent.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/disney-news/\">Disney News: &#8216;Three Men and a Baby&#8217; Reboot, a Superhero Pet Squirrel, More &#8216;Ice Age&#8217;, Animated &#8216;Night at the Museum,&#8217; and Much More</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div et/gh/myreaderx19/cdn6@2020_2/2020/12/12/07-46-09-072_c2e1b6abdc3643ef.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1607759120517},{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"‘Loki’ Trailer Breakdown: The God of Mischief Wreaks Havoc Across All Realities","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649749","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649756\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"loki trailer breakdown\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Loki</em></strong> looks out of this world — this reality, even. And that&#8217;s the intention of the upcoming Disney+ limited series centering around <strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>&#8216;s God of Mischief, who we last saw in <em>Avengers: Endgame</em> stealing the Tesseract and teleporting off to goodness knows where. And it turns out, Loki isn&#8217;t so sure himself, as the trickster god finds himself jumping through time, and various realities, and apparently pursued (and at one point, captured) by a mysterious organization known as the TVA, led by <strong>Owen Wilson</strong>.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a lot to unpack in <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-trailer/\">the jam-packed <em>Loki</em> trailer</a>, so let&#8217;s head into our trailer breakdown.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-649749\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649755\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-1-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-1-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-1-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-1-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-1.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>The trailer starts off with a minute of footage from <em>Avengers: Endgame</em>, leading up to Loki&#8217;s theft of the Tesseract and his disappearance. Then, a flash of weird cosmic lighting that forms some kind of tunnel through space and time, and we cut to: the desert, where a disheveled Loki has landed, just as perplexed as we are. He&#8217;s greeted by three Mongolian-looking people, and his eyes flicker back and forth, apparently considering his options.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649780\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-2-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-2-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-2-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-2-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-2.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649779\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-3-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-3-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-3-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-3-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-3.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Things only get stranger from there, as we cut to the interior of a <del>Marriott Hotel</del> mysterious building that seems to house infinite floors, each with stranger and stranger designations — LK3, 2W1, FHF, VG2, 3FG, CET, XN1, and TSL among them, with peculiar &#8220;x&#8221; and &#8220;=&#8221; signs in the middle, and a symbol that looks like a smiley face. What could they mean? I can&#8217;t say for sure, but if the Marvel Comics depiction of the organization that runs this building, the TVA (or <strong>Time Variance Authority</strong>) is correct, then they each level could house different realities and timelines.</p>\n<p>In the comics, the Time Variance Authority is an organization responsible for monitoring the multiverse and maintaining interdimensional order&#8230;and can even bring an end timelines if they&#8217;re deemed too dangerous to exist. Which makes a trickster god like Loki in possession of a stone that allows him to bend space their worst nightmare.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649778\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-4-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-4-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-4-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-4-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-4.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>&#8220;You taking me somewhere to kill me?&#8221; an imprisoned Loki, wearing a collar and a jumpsuit with the &#8220;TVA&#8221; logo emblazoned on his chest, asks his captor.</p>\n<p>&#8220;No I&#8217;m taking you someplace to talk,&#8221; Owen Wilson&#8217;s cryptic new character wryly responds, to which he and Loki engage in a back-and-forth about the trickster god&#8217;s tendency to lie, going so far as to take a mocking tone with Loki — which proves that Wilson&#8217;s character is one of the few not intimidated by him. So who is Wilson playing? His character was not confirmed at the Disney Investors conference, but — in perhaps a slip of the hand from Marvel — the captions on the trailer for <em>Loki</em> refer to Wilson&#8217;s character as &#8220;Mobius M. Mobius,&#8221; a mid-level manager of the TVA, who is one of dozens of clones (all taking the appearance of long-time Marvel writer/editor, and continuity expert, Mark Gruenwald, in a Marvel meta-joke). This isn&#8217;t confirmation that Wilson is playing Mobius M. Mobius, but it definitely suggests he is — especially with the cropped hair and mustache he shares with the <a href=\"https://comicvine.gamespot.com/mr-mobius/4005-28215/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">comics character</a>.</p>\n<p>More hints are given as to the TVA&#8217;s powers, as Loki asks his captor how long he&#8217;s been there, and Wilson responds, &#8220;It&#8217;s hard to say, you know, time passes differently here in the TVA,&#8221; before pushing him through the elevator doors.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649777\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-5-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-5-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-5-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-5-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-5.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649776\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-6-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-6-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-6-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-6-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-6.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Suddenly we cut to a new setting, where a soldier enters a darkened tent. The trailer is cut in a way that suggests that as soon as Loki was thrust through the elevator doors, he was thrust into a new world (or reality), but that&#8217;s likely a bit of fancy editing. Still, it sets us up for an intriguing series of events, in which a unit of soldiers scope out this darkened outdoor area, lit only by gas lamps.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649775\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-7-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-7-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-7-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-7-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-7.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>This is where things become even more puzzling and difficult to explain. A hooded figure appears, apparently at the same setting that the soldiers are scoping out. The figure carries a gas lamp, which the figure then throws on the ground, lighting the grass on fire.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649774\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-8-700x290.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"290\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-8-700x290.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-8-360x149.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-8-768x318.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-8.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>As the fire spreads, one of the soldiers scrambles away — but he stands out from the rest. The helmet that tumbles off his head bears some resemblance to Captain America&#8217;s World War II helmet, and his uniform bears some parallels to that of the first Avenger&#8217;s, though the bearded brunette man beneath the helmet is clearly not Chris Evans. It&#8217;s possible that this is an alternate version of Captain America, being attacked by the hooded figure. This may confirm the rumors that the villain of the series — and the figure in the hood — is an alternate Loki from a different dimension, who has been <a href=\"https://www.digitalspy.com/tv/ustv/a31663127/loki-richard-e-grant-old/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rumored to be played</a> by <strong>Richard E. Grant</strong>. Grant was confirmed to be part of the <em>Loki</em> cast last night, though Marvel was naturally tight-lipped on his role. However, the hints from this trailer lend nicely to the rumors that Grant is playing Old Man Loki, a villainous future form of Loki from an alternate timeline, who may be set up as the Big Bad for the series.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649773\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-9-700x290.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"290\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-9-700x290.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-9-360x149.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-9-768x318.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-9.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>But we have to be reminded that this Loki in the limited series is not the reformed Loki, but the one still hot off his crimes in <em>The Avengers</em>. He may not be as keen to help the TVA maintain cosmic order, as seen in this shot where Loki is back in his old outfit, looking in the mirror and remarking, &#8220;Glorious.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649772\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-10-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-10-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-10-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-10-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-10.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Back at the TVA, Loki appears to be taken to trial by the organization&#8217;s top authorities, with <strong>Gugu Mbatha-Raw</strong> presiding as judge. Behind her are three faces carved into the wooden wall, which is interesting since, in the comics, the TVA is literally a faceless bureaucracy — most of its agents being artificial clones without faces, sent to monitor each divergent reality. But a few higher-ranking judges enforce the TVA&#8217;s regulations including Justice Peace, Justice Love, Justice Goodwill, Justice Might, Justice Truth, and Justice Liberty. The TVA is also led by a mysterious being known as Mr. Alternity.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649771\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-11-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-11-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-11-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-11-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-11.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Mbatha-Raw may be playing one of these justices — who, in the comics, sometimes have a tendency to go rogue and commit the crimes they&#8217;re meant to prevent. Which may explain a later scene which sees Mbatha-Raw&#8217;s character, flanked by two agents, fighting with Loki.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649770\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-12-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-12-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-12-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-12-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-12.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>More sculptures within this seemingly infinite TVA building. I&#8217;m guessing they&#8217;re the same three figures in the courtroom.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649768\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-14-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-14-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-14-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-14-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-14.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>In another sequence with the imprisoned Loki, he&#8217;s shown scenes of the lead-up to his capture by the Avengers over a hologram, which Loki turns his head away from, in shame. It suggests Loki is captured soon after he teleported away with the Tesseract, his defeat still fresh.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649767\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-15-700x290.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"290\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-15-700x290.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-15-360x149.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-15-768x318.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-15.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>But an interesting turn of events takes place halfway through the trailer: Loki appears to be working with the TVA, or at least accompanying them on a mission at a store called &#8220;Boxxcart,&#8221; where the agents take down a man for crimes unknown.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649765\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-17-700x290.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"290\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-17-700x290.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-17-360x149.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-17-768x318.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-17.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>In one of the most intriguing shots of the trailer Wilson&#8217;s character (who may or may not be Mobius M. Mobius), hands something over to a little white-haired girl, as they stand under the refracted light shining through a stained glass window pane of a demonic figure surrounded by cosmic imagery. Who is this ethereal-looking girl? A guardian of some dimension or reality? One that is evil, considering the demonic figure on the glass? It&#8217;s too hard to say for now, but it&#8217;s clear that <em>Loki</em> is stepping up its visuals in a big way.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649766\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-16-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-16-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-16-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-16-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-16.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Loki is getting tossed around the TVA a lot, landing in a depot with a metal detector covered in some red paint, standing over a scorched piece of floor. Another TVA staff member glances at Loki with mild annoyance as Loki appears to look for a way out.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649764\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-18-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-18-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-18-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-18-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-18.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Speaking of stepping up the visuals, look at this gorgeous, cosmic image of what appears to be a planet or moon crumbling to pieces. Perhaps an effect of Loki&#8217;s reality-warping mischief?</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649763\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-19-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-19-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-19-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-19-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-19.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Apparently beneath that crumbling moon/asteroid/planet, sits a young girl in the ruins of her planet, bathed in a purple light. The next shot shows meteors showering down on this same planet surface. There&#8217;s also the possibility that this is one of the instances when the TVA puts a &#8220;stop&#8221; to timelines considered too dangerous to exist.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649762\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-20-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-20-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-20-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-20-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-20.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Loki, in the TVA jacket we saw him in before while accompanying the agents into the Boxxcart store, stands among the ruins of a city. It&#8217;s another stunning, intriguing piece of imagery that I can&#8217;t make heads or tails of.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649761\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-21-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-21-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-21-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-21-768x321.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-21.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>But in one fo the most fun twists of the trailer, we see Loki board a plane as D.B. Cooper — yes, <a href=\"https://www.fbi.gov/history/famous-cases/db-cooper-hijacking\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>that</em></a> D.B. Cooper. The man behind the hijacking of the Boeing 727 aircraft in 1971, who managed to extort $200,000 in ransom money and parachute out of the airplane, never to be seen again. The manhunt for Cooper and his disappearance has remained one of the greatest unsolved cases of the 20th century, but here we get a magical little spin on it: that Loki was D.B. Cooper, and that his disappearance is explained by Heimdall suddenly beaming him up to Asgard as he jumps out of the plane.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649759\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-23-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-23-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-23-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-23-768x321.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-23.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>When <em>Loki</em> was first announced, we&#8217;d heard many descriptions of it being a &#8220;time-hopping&#8221; adventure, and thus far we&#8217;d seen little of that, except for the D.B. Cooper scene. But in a short scene of Loki tossing a tunic-wearing woman out of the way, we get another glimpse of what appears to be a historical setting that the god of mischief has found himself in (still wearing the TVA agent gear).</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649758\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-24-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-24-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-24-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-24-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-24.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Has Loki become an agent for the TVA, finding himself in increasingly absurd situations? That seems to be the case with this one sequence which sees a man dressed remarkably like M&#8217;Baku from <em>Black Panther</em> taking a hammer to a Loki lookalike, knocking the antler helm off his head, as the real Loki looks on in shock behind the fray. There are vines and wreckage bursting through ceilings and walls of this room, which suggests realities colliding in some way.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649756\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-700x292.jpg\" alt=\"loki trailer breakdown\" width=\"700\" height=\"292\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-700x292.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26-768x320.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-trailer-breakdown-26.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>The final scene of the trailer, in which Loki wears a green suit and his antler helm, with a political &#8220;Loki&#8221; sticker on his chest, appears to be a deliberate nod to the <em>Vote Loki</em> comic book arc by Christopher Hastings, a four-part 2016 comic book run that parodied the 2016 presidential elections and followed Loki&#8217;s controversial political campaign for President of the United States.</p>\n<p>Another alternate reality that Loki finds himself in? Or perhaps a sign of the decaying barriers between realities, as he is in the same destroyed room as before (filled with artifacts from across history) surrounded by various historical warriors, also wearing Loki stickers, who quickly turn on the Norse god after he smugly remarks, &#8220;What did you expect?&#8221;</p>\n<p>We don&#8217;t know what we expected, nor what to expect, when <em>Loki</em> hits Disney+ in <strong>May 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-trailer-breakdown/\">&#8216;Loki&#8217; Trailer Breakdown: The God of Mischief Wreaks Havoc Across All Realities</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"‘Thor: Love and Thunder’ Will Return Jaimie Alexander’s Lady Sif to the MCU","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649906","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-649925 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Lady-Sif-returns-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Lady Sif returns\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Lady-Sif-returns.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Lady-Sif-returns-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Jaimie Alexander</strong> is about to make her return to the Marvel Cinematic Universe.</p>\n<p>After being a part of the first two <em>Thor</em> films but not appearing in 2017&#8217;s <em>Thor: Ragnarok</em>, a new report says Alexander will be coming back to reprise her role as the Asgardian warrior Lady Sif in writer/director <strong>Taika Waititi</strong>&#8216;s upcoming sequel <em><strong>Thor: Love and Thunder</strong></em>. And there&#8217;s one other place she might pop up, too.<br />\n<span id=\"more-649906\"></span></p>\n<p>Deadline reports that Alexander is set to return to the MCU in <em>Thor: Love and Thunder</em>, the new film from Taika Waititi which will introduce <strong>Christian Bale</strong> to the franchise <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/christian-bale-thor-love-and-thunder-villain-gorr-the-god-butcher/\">as the villainous Gorr the God Butcher</a>. The report also states that Sif might have a guest spot in <strong><em>Loki</em></strong>, the Disney+ series in which <strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>&#8216;s villain criss-crosses through time. That makes sense, given that Sif first appeared in <em>Thor</em>, the project which introduced Loki in the MCU, and the two have already come face to face on screen before.</p>\n<p>Alexander&#8217;s Lady Sif also appeared in <em>Thor: The Dark World </em>and two episodes of the TV series <em>Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.</em>, and she was evidently a fan favorite. But frankly – and this was no fault of the actress – Sif simply didn&#8217;t have enough to do in those early <em>Thor</em> movies for her to leave much of an imprint in my mind. Thankfully, Taika Waititi injected the self-serious and occasionally dour <em>Thor</em> franchise with a much-needed dose of humor with <em>Thor: Ragnarok</em>, and elevated that franchise out of the MCU gutter and more toward top-tier material. Here&#8217;s hoping he&#8217;ll be able to give Sif much more to chew on this time around than she&#8217;s had before.</p>\n<p>Alexander, who recently starred on the NBC series <em>Blindspot</em>, won&#8217;t be the only woman returning to the <em>Thor</em> franchise in this next entry. <strong>Natalie Portman</strong>, who also sat out the events of <em>Thor: Ragnarok</em>, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/thor-love-thunder-will-give-natalie-portman-a-different-version-of-thors-powers/\">will be back</a> in <em>Thor: Love and Thunder</em>, and she&#8217;ll be wielding the powerful hammer Mjolnir as a superhero known as The Mighty Thor. She&#8217;ll presumably be taking the mantle because <strong>Chris Hemsworth</strong>, who is coming back to reprise the title role, will likely be off spending some time in space with his new pals, the Guardians of the Galaxy. <strong>Chris Pratt</strong>&#8216;s Peter Quill (AKA Star-Lord) <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/thor-love-and-thunder-cast-chris-pratt/\">is showing up</a> in this new movie, and we expect more Guardians to be announced soon as well.</p>\n<p>Production on the new sequel is set to start next month.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/lady-sif-returns-to-the-mcu/\">&#8216;Thor: Love and Thunder&#8217; Will Return Jaimie Alexander&#8217;s Lady Sif to the MCU</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=JVYxkRZbHak:YGwPUWjwLQA:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img Bomb","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=648987","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/amanda-seyfreid-guardians-of-the-galaxy.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-648996\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/amanda-seyfreid-guardians-of-the-galaxy-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"amanda seyfried guardians of the galaxy\" width=\"700\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/amanda-seyfreid-guardians-of-the-galaxy-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/amanda-seyfreid-guardians-of-the-galaxy-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/amanda-seyfreid-guardians-of-the-galaxy.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Amanda Seyfried</strong> never really went away, exactly, but she&#8217;s been having herself a nice little &#8220;comeback&#8221; recently. She&#8217;s turned in great work in films like <em>First Reformed</em>, <em>Twin Peaks</em>, and this year&#8217;s <em>Mank</em> (and, yes, the <em>Mama Mia!</em> films). And at one point, she was almost part of the Marvel Cinematic Universe, too. Seyfried has previously commented on turning down the role of Gamora in James Gunn&#8217;s <strong><em>Guardians of the Galaxy</em></strong>, and in a new interview, she goes into more detail as to why: she was worried the movie was going to bomb.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-648987\"></span></p>\n<p>Once upon a time, Amanda Seyfried almost played Gamora in Guardians<em> of the Galaxy</em>. She turned the part down, though, and has said in the past she didn&#8217;t want to sit in a make-up chair for hours for the part. &#8220;I was just like, &#8216;Ah, I don’t wanna be green. It&#8217;s just so much work,'&#8221; Seyfried told <a href=\"https://heroichollywood.com/amanda-seyfried-guardians-of-the-galaxy-gamora-passed-role/\">ComicBook</a> earlier this year. &#8220;I remember Jennifer Lawrence talking about once, how long it took her to get blue [for the <em>X-Men</em> movies]. And I was like, &#8216;That seems like hell on earth,&#8217; because then you get to set and you&#8217;re only there for a couple hours, and then you have to take everything off. And that was literally the reason.&#8221;</p>\n<p>But in a new interview with <a href=\"https://www.stitcher.com/show/awards-chatter/episode/amanda-seyfried-mank-79901490\">THR</a> (via <a href=\"https://www.indiewire.com/2020/12/amanda-seyfried-rejected-guardians-of-the-galaxy-box-office-bomb-1234603056/\">IndieWire</a>), Seyfried gave another reason for passing on the MCU: fear of failure. &#8220;I didn&#8217;t want to be part of the first Marvel movie that bombed,&#8221; Seyfried said. &#8220;I said, &#8216;Who wants to see a movie about a talking tree and a raccoon?&#8217; Which is clearly — I was very wrong.&#8221;</p>\n<p>While Seyfried&#8217;s decision seems short-sighted right now, she definitely had a point at the time. While the Marvel brand was strong before <em>Guardians of the Galaxy</em> came out, there was some concern that the movie would not find an audience. While previous Marvel movies had focused on characters that were pretty well known – Iron Man, Captain America, and so on – the Guardians weren&#8217;t exactly household names at the time. It really looked like a risk for Marvel. Of course, we now know it all worked out in the end – <em>Guardians of the Galaxy</em> ended up being the third-highest-grossing film of 2014.</p>\n<p>But Seyfried didn&#8217;t know that at the time. &#8220;The script was great, it was all based in not wanting to be &#8216;that guy,'&#8221; she added in the new interview. &#8220;Because if you are the star of a giant movie like that, and it bombs, Hollywood does not forgive you. I’ve seen that happen to people and it was a giant, giant fear and I thought, is it worth it?&#8221;</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"‘Ambulance’, the Latest From Michael Bay, Adds Yahya Abdul-Mateen II Alongside Jake Gyllenhaal","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649910","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649931\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"ambulance cast Yahya Abdul-Mateen II\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Yahya Abdul-Mateen II</strong> is catching a ride on <strong>Michael Bay</strong>&#8216;s <strong><em>Ambulance</em></strong>. The actor, who recently appeared in <em>The Trial of the Chicago 7</em> and will next be seen in <em>Candyman</em>, is joining <strong>Jake Gyllenhaal</strong> in the action-thriller about thieves who steal an ambulance as their getaway vehicle, only to then realize there&#8217;s a sick patient still in the back.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-649910\"></span></p>\n<p>Yahya Abdul-Mateen II has quickly risen to be one of those must-watch actors. He stole the show in <em>Aquaman</em>, had a brief-but-memorable turn in <em>Us</em>, was great on <em>Watchmen</em>, and he delivers arguably the best performance in <em>The Trial of the Chicago 7</em>, a film loaded with wall-to-wall great actors. And now he wants in on some Bayhem. THR is reporting that Abdul-Mateen is joining Jake Gyllenhaal in Michael Bay&#8217;s <em>Ambulance</em>.</p>\n<p>The movie is a remake of the 2005 Danish film <em>Ambulancen</em>, in which two brothers commit a robbery to pay for an operation for their dying mother. They end up hijacking an ambulance, only to then realize that a dying heart transplant patient and a hospital intern are both in the back of the vehicle. The script for the remake, penned by Chris Fedak, has been floating around for a while, with this synopsis:</p>\n<blockquote><p>A vet just back from Afghanistan is drawn by his brother into a bank robbery in downtown Los Angeles. When the robbery goes horribly wrong, the brothers take hostages and hijack an ambulance. As the situation escalates, old wounds reopen in the relationship between the brothers as they fight to survive what seems like an impossible situation.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Now, according to <strong>THR</strong>, the script has undergone a rewrite so that the lead characters are no longer brothers, opening the door for Abdul-Mateen to play Gyllenhaal&#8217;s partner in crime. The plot remains mostly the same, and in addition to the sick patient in the back, there&#8217;s also a paramedic. The paramedic part will be played by <strong>Eiza González </strong><em>(Baby</em> <em>Driver</em>)<em>.</em></p>\n<p>As previously <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ambulance-jake-gyllenhaal/\">reported</a>, the film is said to have the potential to recall &#8220;great action thrillers of the ’90s like <em>Speed</em> and Bay’s <em>Bad Boys</em>,&#8221; so it makes sense that Bay is drawn to this. I think Bay <em>can</em> turn in a good film now and then – I&#8217;ll admit it, I love <em>The Rock – </em>but he also delivers plenty of junk. I couldn&#8217;t even make it through <em>6 Underground</em>. Hopefully, <em>Ambulance</em> turns out to be one of his better offerings. Throwing Gyllenhaal and Abdul-Mateen into the mix certainly doesn&#8217;t hurt.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ambulance-cast-yahya-abdul-mateen-ii/\">&#8216;Ambulance&#8217;, the Latest From Michael Bay, Adds Yahya Abdul-Mateen II Alongside Jake Gyllenhaal</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=A1qQTJAmW0U:yqywJVu4Orc:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 23:00:16 +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ambulance-cast-Yahya-Abdul-Mateen-II-700x321.jpg","linkMd5":"fd577f2b93299d70c6fbf3d0dad39c83","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn26@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-45-35-036_0b57be6c1032f678.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":321,"sourceBytes":33591,"destBytes":21650,"author":"Chris 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"Is Marvel Studios Building Toward a Young Avengers Movie?","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649844","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649872\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/young-avengers-1-e1607716609561-700x372.jpg\" alt=\"young avengers\" width=\"700\" height=\"372\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/young-avengers-1-e1607716609561-700x372.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/young-avengers-1-e1607716609561-360x191.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/young-avengers-1-e1607716609561-768x408.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/young-avengers-1-e1607716609561.jpg 790w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><i>Avengers: Endgame</i> brought an end of an era — one that changed up who would take on the mantle of Earth&#8217;s mightiest heroes. There are already several beloved superheroes and galactic teams jostling for that responsibility, but what about the next generation? The children are the future, after all, and — thanks to a five-year time jump — they&#8217;re all grown up.</p>\n<p><strong>The Young Avengers </strong>—a group of superhero protégés who came together in the comics to save the world after the main adult team broke apart — has been <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/mcu-future-young-avengers-lgbt-kevin-feige/\">teased and rumored</a> heavily for the past few years. But for the first time, with the confirmation of core team members like Kate Bishop (<strong>Hailee Steinfeld</strong>), Cassie Lang (<strong>Kathryn Newton</strong>), and America Chavez (<strong>Xochitl Gomez</strong>), we&#8217;re seeing serious steps on Marvel Studios&#8217; part to bring them together.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-649844\"></span></p>\n<p>The next Hawkeye, Scott Lang&#8217;s daughter and protége, and a super-strong Latin-American teen may form the core of Marvel Studios&#8217; Young Avengers. Or at least, it seems that&#8217;s the direction that the Marvel Cinematic Universe is headed, with the introduction of <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/hailee-steinfeld-as-kate-bishop/\">Hailee Steinfeld as Kate Bishop</a>, the younger Hawkeye who will be seen teaming up with Jeremy Renner&#8217;s archer in the Disney+ series <em>Hawkeye;</em> the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/america-chavez-mcu/\">confirmation of America Chavez</a>, as played by <em>The Babysitters Club</em> star Xochitl Gomez, in <em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em>; and the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ant-man-3-title/\">recasting of Cassie Lang</a> with <em>Freaky</em> breakout Kathryn Newton. These castings were all confirmed at the Disney Investors conference Thursday, and hint that a Young Avengers team-up is surely inevitable.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-629982\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/hawkeye-katebishop-conceptart-highres-frontpage-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Hawkeye - Kate Bishop Concept Art\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/hawkeye-katebishop-conceptart-highres-frontpage.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/hawkeye-katebishop-conceptart-highres-frontpage-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Who are the Young Avengers (So Far)?</h2>\n<p><strong>Kate Bishop</strong>, and <strong>Cassie Lang</strong> were two of the core members of the Young Avengers, a team of teen superheroes who first got together in series by Allan Heinberg and Jim Cheung. After the events of the 2004–2005 &#8220;Avengers Disassembled&#8221; storyline, these teens decided to fill the hole left by the dissolution of the main Avengers team. If the adults weren&#8217;t going to save the world, the kids would.</p>\n<p>Kate Bishop was a rich debutante-turned-archer vigilante who would make a name for herself as Hawkeye before being taken under Clint Barton&#8217;s wing. Meanwhile, Cassie Lang had the same powers as her father Scott Lang, the power to change size at will, taking on the name Stature.</p>\n<p><strong>America Chavez</strong> (also known as Miss America), a super-strong alien with the power to fly and create portals between universe with her kicks, would join as a lead member in the new <em>Young Avengers</em> series by Kieron Gillen and drawn by Jamie McKelvie, which launched in 2013. She would become the first major Latin-American LGBTQ character in Marvel Comics and quickly establish a rapport (and arguably, romantic tension) with Kate Bishop in the second Young Avengers line-up.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-620529\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ironheart-conceptart-rafgrassetti-700x332.jpg\" alt=\"Ironheart Artwork\" width=\"700\" height=\"332\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ironheart-conceptart-rafgrassetti-700x332.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ironheart-conceptart-rafgrassetti-360x171.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ironheart-conceptart-rafgrassetti-768x364.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ironheart-conceptart-rafgrassetti.jpg 1080w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Who Else Could Join?</h2>\n<p>Kate Bishop will be joining the MCU through the Disney+ series <em>Hawkeye</em>, while Cassie Lang and America Chavez will both get big-screen time with <em>Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania</em> and <em>Doctor Strange</em><em> in the Multiverse of Madness</em>, respectively. Notably,<strong> Kang the Conqueror</strong> (<strong>Jonathan Majors</strong>) — a notorious foe for the Young Avengers — will be the main villain of <em>Ant-Man 3</em>, which suggests that <em>Quantumania</em> may be our big lead-in to this team-up. In the comics, a young version of Kang, before he becomes a villain, time travels back to join the young Avengers as Iron Lad, leading to the Young Avengers facing the dilemma of realizing their team member is destined to be a villain.</p>\n<p>With the forthcoming <em>Loki</em> series potentially dealing with alternate realities and alternate Lokis, there&#8217;s a chance that we could be introduced to <strong>Young Loki</strong>, another core member of the Young Avengers team, albeit one who is taken on as part-hostage, part-wary ally. I wouldn&#8217;t be surprised if <em>Loki</em> ended with the introduction of Young Loki, ripe for a Young Avengers team-up.</p>\n<p>And while this character hasn&#8217;t been associated with Young Avengers before, the announcement of an <strong><em>Ironheart</em></strong> series, which follow the character of Riri Williams (a young Black girl who’s a genius inventor who creates a suit of armor that rivals Tony Stark&#8217;s) suggests we may see the character played by <strong>Dominique Thorne </strong>join the team.</p>\n<p>With Iron Man dead and Captain America retired, and the rest of the main Avengers doing their own spin-off shows before likely retiring too, there&#8217;s a huge void that the Young Avengers are primed to fill. And Marvel Studios is putting all of the pieces in place.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/marvel-studios-young-avengers/\">Is Marvel Studios Building Toward a Young Avengers Movie?</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Originals","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649825","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-531824 aligncenter\" /></p>\n<p>Without San Diego Comic-Con, New York Comic-Con, Star Wars Celebration or any big media events, Disney was left to announce tons of news during their big livestreamed presentation for investors last night. That means some little tidbits got lost in the shuffle, such as Disney announcing their plans to make Hulu the exclusive streaming home to original movies from 20th Century Studios and Searchlight, the studios formerly known as 20th Century Fox and Fox Searchlight.<span id=\"more-649825\"></span></p>\n<p>Following the success of original movies like <em>Palm Springs</em>, <em>Bad Hair</em>, and <em>Run</em> this year, Hulu President <strong>Kelly Campbell</strong> announced the streaming service&#8217;s slate of original movies would expand with offerings they&#8217;ll co-produce with 20th Century Studios and Searchlight Pictures, which came with their acquisition of 21st Century Fox.</p>\n<p>What&#8217;s not clear is if these movies from 20th Century Studios and Searchlight Pictures will be streaming exclusive titles or if they&#8217;ll be released in theaters and be branded as Hulu originals. The three aforementioned titles played on Hulu only, but it&#8217;s not clear if that would have been the case if the coronavirus pandemic hadn&#8217;t struck such a blow to movie theaters this year.</p>\n<p>Considering the recent move by Warner Bros. to <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/warner-bros-2021/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">send movies to HBO Max</a> the same day they hit theaters in 2021, and Disney beefing up their Disney+ Premier Access offerings, maybe there&#8217;s a chance Disney will have 20th Century Studios and Searchlight Pictures do some hybrid theatrical and streaming releases of their own? If not, maybe Hulu is just following in the same footsteps as Disney+ by having more original movies produced solely for streaming.</p>\n<p>Hulu said more details on this deal would be revealed in the coming months. The first 20th Century Studios title in 2021 is <em>The King&#8217;s Man</em> in January, followed by <em>Everybody&#8217;s Talking About Jamie</em> in February and there have been rumblings about the former going to Hulu and the latter possibly to Disney+. Meanwhile, Searchlight has both <em>Antlers</em> and <em>Nomadland</em> intended for release in February, and those could easily get streaming releases on Hulu. We&#8217;ll be sure to keep you posted when more details surface.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\"
