1080w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia</em></strong> was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/its-always-sunny-season-15-renewal/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">recently renewed for season 15</a> at FX (or FXX), but the cable comedy series is actually sticking around for a lot longer than that. The series created by star <strong>Rob McElhenney</strong> has officially been renewed for four more seasons, which will be enough to not only break the record as the longest-running live-action comedy series in American television history, but completely shatter it.<span id=\"more-649420\"></span></p>\n<p>Previously, McElhenney said negotiations were underway for season 15 and season 16, but apparently FX couldn&#8217;t help but order season 17 and season 18 along with &#8217;em. The 15th season is what will officially make the series a longer-running live-action comedy than the previous record holder, <em>The Adventures of Ozzie &#38; Harriet</em>.</p>\n<p>However, it should be noted that the classic ABC series ran for a total of 435 episodes across 14 seasons, with each season having anywhere between 25 and 39 episodes, so <em>It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia</em> has a lot of catching up to do on that front. Even if each of the new four seasons has the standard 10-episode run the series has stuck to since the eighth season, that won&#8217;t even bring their total to half of that count. Thankfully, Rob McElhenney has plans for much more. He wrote on Twitter yesterday:</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Sunny was originally pitched as a 36 season arc. So happy to be halfway done. <a href=\"https://t.co/xT7US6RPnP\">https://t.co/xT7US6RPnP</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Rob McElhenney (@RMcElhenney) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RMcElhenney/status/1337174807431925767?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 10, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Obviously he&#8217;s joking about having an initial pitch for a show that long, but if there&#8217;s any series that has the perfect formula to make a run for that long,<em> It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia</em> is certainly it. Co-star Glenn Howerton agrees completely, whether you like it or not. He wrote on Twitter:</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We will pummel you all into submission with this show. We will ram it down your dirty throats! <a href=\"https://t.co/1nf95pNgGR\">https://t.co/1nf95pNgGR</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Glenn with two n’s (@GlennHowerton) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GlennHowerton/status/1337190917917163520?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 11, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Earlier this year, McElhenney addressed whether or not the next season of <em>It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia</em> would address the coronavirus pandemic, but he reminded everyone that they actually already did a pandemic episode of sorts:</p>\n<blockquote><p>“Well, we actually do have an episode called ‘The Gang Gets Quarantined’ [in season 9] where we quarantine ourselves in the bar. I think there’s a big flu going around Philadelphia or something like that. When we come back, don’t worry, we will address all this in the way only <em>Sunny</em> can!&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Considering how despicable the characters of <em>It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia</em> are in every single episode, we can only imagine how they&#8217;d react to a situation like the coronavirus pandemic. We&#8217;re not sure when the new season will arrive on FX (or FXX), but we&#8217;ll be ready for their increasingly questionable antics whenever they actually make their return.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/its-always-sunny-in-philadelphia-renewed-for-4-seasons/\">&#8216;It&#8217;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia&#8217; Gets Four More Seasons from FX</a> +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/itsalwayssunny-season14-bar-watchingtv-700x338.jpg","linkMd5":"3e2a658eb4ce26976ffb4865462c57d4","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn17@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-34-839_b2ed5651cdeefcad.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":338,"sourceBytes":43759,"destBytes":29220,"author":"Ethan Anderton","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/itsalwayssunny-season14-bar-watchingtv-700x338.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn17@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-34-839_b2ed5651cdeefcad.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn26@2020_5/2020/12/12/07-46-09-160_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=cFhbBMgQprI:ZQyDVZz5wf0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn14@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-07-341_e84f0e6c301bf156.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn21@2020_5/2020/12/12/07-46-11-127_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=cFhbBMgQprI:ZQyDVZz5wf0:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn2@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-10-652_0506c45003ca688c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/cFhbBMgQprI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn50@2020_6/2020/12/12/07-46-08-563_d50250086805e53a.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1607759120493},{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"Christopher Nolan Loves the ‘Fast and Furious’ Movies, Especially the Original","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649272","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-303712 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Christopher-Nolan-directing-The-Dark-Knight-Rises-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Christopher Nolan Directing James Bond\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Christopher-Nolan-directing-The-Dark-Knight-Rises-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Christopher-Nolan-directing-The-Dark-Knight-Rises-360x155.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Christopher Nolan</strong> is one of the most acclaimed blockbuster filmmakers in the game, and he has a vibe that sometimes feels a little stuffy, even if he&#8217;s not necessarily cold in real life. For example, many were shocked to learn that Nolan is a huge fan of the goofy comedy <em>MacGruber</em>, so much that he even <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/christopher-nolans-macgruber-e-mail/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sent an e-mail wishing luck to everyone</a> when production on Peacock&#8217;s sequel series pilot began. Now we&#8217;re learning that Nolan likes his junk food action cinema too, because he&#8217;s admitted to liking the <strong><em>Fast ad Furious</em></strong> movies, especially the original from 2001.<span id=\"more-649272\"></span></p>\n<p>Appearing on the <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/happy-sad-confused/id827905050\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Happy Sad Confused podcast</a>, Nolan was asked about a rumor that he&#8217;s a fan of the <em>Fast and Furious</em> franchise starring <strong>Vin Diesel </strong>and his ensemble of &#8220;family&#8221; members that has helped him through the thick, the thin, and the absolutely insane. Nolan actually likes how the movies have been getting bigger and crazier, even though he likes a couple of the early entries in the franchise more. Here&#8217;s what Nolan had to say (via <a href=\"https://comicbook.com/movies/news/the-dark-knight-director-chris-nolan-fast-furious-movies/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">ComicBook.com</a>):</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I’m sort of an original recipe [guy], I mean the Rob Cohen original&#8230; But I’ve got a very soft spot for Tokyo Drift, actually. And then the skill as Justin Lin’s iterations, as they got crazier and bigger and crazier and bigger, they became something else, but something else kind of fun. The fun thing about those movies is even as they’ve gotten bigger and bigger and bigger, as sequels have to do, everyone always complains that sequels get bigger but we’re the people making sequels get bigger, we do want them bigger, you don’t want them smaller, it’s the Alien 3 lesson that [director David] Fincher learned. You can do it but it’s not going to make anybody happy, even though personally I love that film, a lot more than he does in fact.”</p></blockquote>\n<p>Though <em>Tokyo Drift </em>was panned upon release, it has since become a favorite of longtime fans, even without the presence of Vin Diesel or Paul Walker in the lead roles.</p>\n<p>But all good things must come to an end, and we only have three more movies in the <em>Fast and Furious</em> franchise to look forward to. Originally intended for release earlier this year, <em>F9</em> will be drifting into theaters on <strong>May 28, 2021</strong>. Then the franchise will be coming to a close <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/fast-and-furious-franchise-ending-with-two-part-finale/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">with a two-film finale</a> directed by <strong>Justin Lin</strong>. That means when the <em>Fast and Furious</em> franchise concludes, the movies will have literally turned it up to 11. And if they don&#8217;t work that into the marketing, someone should be fired.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s hoping we can keep finding out movies that Christopher Nolan loves. Maybe we should start taking bets. Could Nolan secretly be a fan of the <em>Big Momma&#8217;s House</em> movies?</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/christopher-nolan-loves-the-fast-and-furious-movies/\">Christopher Nolan Loves the &#8216;Fast and Furious&#8217; Movies, Especially the Original</a> appeared first on 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"Movie Release Dates: ‘Free Guy’ Moves to May, ‘Death on the Nile’ Floats to September, ‘Antlers’ Vanishes Entirely","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649790","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-27-1.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-649796\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-27-1-700x394.jpg\" alt=\"Free Guy Release Date\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-27-1-700x394.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-27-1-360x203.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-27-1-768x432.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Yesterday, Disney held their huge, exhausting Investors Day presentation, and while they announced plenty of stuff, they didn&#8217;t cover <em>everything</em>. For instance: three upcoming Disney-adjacent films – <strong><em>Free Guy</em></strong>, with <strong>Ryan Reynolds</strong>, <strong>Kenneth Branagh</strong>&#8216;s <em><strong>Death on the Nile</strong></em>, and the horror film <strong><em>Antlers</em></strong> – received no mention. But now we have some updates. Both <em>Free Guy</em> and <em>Death on the Nile</em> have changed their release dates yet again, while <em>Antlers</em> has vanished from the calendar entirely.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-649790\"></span></p>\n<p>Sure, we got a ton of news about Marvel, Pixar, <em>Star Wars</em>, and other Disney-related stuff yesterday. But what of the lonely world of Fox? Disney owns Fox now (in case you forgot), which means they own upcoming movies <em>Free Guy</em>, <em>Death on the Nile</em>, and <em>Antlers</em>. But since those movies didn&#8217;t really fit in with the brand synergy the House of Mouse was selling yesterday, they went unremarked upon. Today, though, Disney shuffled their release dates.</p>\n<p>First: <em>Free Guy</em>. Directed by <strong>Shawn Levy</strong> and starring Ryan Reynolds, <em>Free Guy </em>follows a bank teller called Guy who &#8220;realizes he is a background character in an open world video game called Free City that will soon go offline.&#8221; The film was supposed to hit theaters on July 3, 2020, but of course, that didn&#8217;t happen due to the coronavirus. So Disney moved it to December 11, 2020 – and then pulled it from the release date calendar entirely. Now, it&#8217;s back, with a new date for 2021 – <strong>May 2, 2021</strong>, to be precise.</p>\n<p>Then there&#8217;s <em>Death on the Nile</em>. This is Kenneth Branagh&#8217;s follow-up to <em>Murder on the Orient Express</em>, and once again, Branagh is playing famed detective Hercule Poirot. In the first film, Poirot had to solve a crime on a moving train. Here, a murder happens on a boat. And, like the first film, Branagh is backed-up by a cast of famous faces: <strong>Russell Brand</strong>, <strong>Gal Gadot</strong>, <strong>Armie Hammer</strong>, <strong>Rose Leslie</strong>, <strong>Letitia Wright</strong>, and more. Believe it or not, once upon a time Disney planned on releasing this on December 20, 2019. Then they changed it to October 9, 2020. Then it got pushed two more times: first to October 23, and again to December 18. Then, just like <em>Free Guy</em>, it got pulled from the calendar entirely. There was some speculation that <em>Death on the Nile</em> might go to Disney+, but instead, Disney has now given it a <strong>September 7, 2021</strong> release date.</p>\n<p>Finally, there&#8217;s <em>Antlers</em>, the only title in this story I&#8217;m actually interested in seeing. So of course, it&#8217;s the one title that has no new release date at all. Directed by <strong>Scott Cooper</strong> and produced by <strong>Guillermo del Toro</strong>, this horror film involves a mysterious creature terrorizing a small town. It was supposed to open on April 17, 2020, then got pushed to February 19, 2021. Now, it&#8217;s off the calendar entirely. If I had to guess, I would wager that Disney might be considering releasing this one straight to Hulu. Both <em>Free Guy</em> and <em>Death on the Nile</em> are bigger movies with bigger stars, and Disney obviously wants to keep them theatrical. <em>Antlers</em>, however, is a smaller, R-rated horror film, so I wouldn&#8217;t be surprised if it went to streaming. Or perhaps that&#8217;s just wishful thinking on my part, because I&#8217;d sure like to see this thing sooner rather than later.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/free-guy-release-date/\">Movie Release Dates: &#8216;Free Guy&#8217; Moves to May, &#8216;Death on the Nile&#8217; Floats to September, &#8216;Antlers&#8217; Vanishes Entirely</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 15:45:20","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:20","title":"Pixar’s ‘Soul’ Clips: Joe Gardner Teaches Band Class and Zones Out While Tickling the Ivories","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=649071","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-647870 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/soul-joegardner-piano-inthezone-colorful-700x319.jpg\" alt=\"Soul Featurette\" width=\"700\" height=\"319\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/soul-joegardner-piano-inthezone-colorful-700x319.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/soul-joegardner-piano-inthezone-colorful-360x164.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/soul-joegardner-piano-inthezone-colorful-768x350.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/soul-joegardner-piano-inthezone-colorful.jpg 1192w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Christmas will bring us two cinematic gifts to keep us occupied during what will probably be the weirdest and saddest holiday season that we&#8217;ve had in awhile. <em>Wonder Woman 1984</em> will arrive on HBO Max the same day that it hits theaters, and Disney is releasing Pixar&#8217;s <strong><em>Soul</em></strong> on Disney+ at no extra charge. Since we&#8217;ve been seeing so much from the former recently, it&#8217;s time to get a new look at the latter with a new clip that shows off the incredible piano skills of Joe Gardner (<strong>Jamie Foxx</strong>).<span id=\"more-649071\"></span></p>\n<h2>Pixar&#8217;s Soul Clips</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/DRNPg-xPoZc?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>In this first clip, which opens the movie, we get to see how Joe Gardner tries to bring a little passion to his middle school band class. If you were ever in band in school, you know exactly what this classroom is like. But there&#8217;s always some glimmer of musical hope in a few students, and Joe sees that here, even if he&#8217;s not entirely satisfied with his job. Thankfully, there&#8217;s a new opportunity that comes his way.</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/x19uk5g71zI?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Joe Gardner gets to tickle the ivories in an impressive way when he sits down to audition for <span class=\"aCOpRe\">legendary jazz musician Dorothea Williams (<strong>Angela Bassett</strong>) </span>and her quartet that&#8217;s playing at <span class=\"aCOpRe\">The Half Note Club in New York City. Dorothea laments the fact that they&#8217;re relegated to hearing a middle school band teacher audition to fill a spot in their group, but she changes her tune completely when Gardner plays a bit of improvised music on the piano, finally landing him the kind of gig he&#8217;s been yearning to get for years. </span></p>\n<p>This is one of those sequences that shows off how incredible the animation in <em>Soul</em> really is. Aside from bringing piano playing to life in a surreal visual representation, the dimly lit environment of the club perfectly captures the essence of a hole-in-the-wall jazz venue like that. The instruments themselves look like they were plucked from reality, from the shimmer on the saxophone to the veneer on the bass. Pixar is the best at what they do for a reason.</p>\n<p>If you&#8217;d like to learn more about<em> Soul</em>, be sure to <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/pixars-soul-interview-pete-docter-kemp-powers-dana-murray/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">check out our interview</a> with director <strong>Pete Docter</strong>, co-director/writer <strong>Kemp Powers</strong>, and producer <strong>Dana Murray</strong>. You can also learn about some of the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/pixars-soul-story-development/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">alternate versions of the movie</a> that Pixar developed throughout their long production process, and dig deeper into the making of the movie <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-making-of-pixars-soul-from-the-real-world-to-the-great-before-and-beyond/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over here</a>.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the official synopsis for Pixar&#8217;s <em>Soul</em>:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p data-pw-in-article=\"true\"><span class=\"style-scope yt-formatted-string\" dir=\"auto\">Joe Gardner (Jamie Foxx) is a middle-school band teacher who gets the chance of a lifetime to play at the best jazz club in town. But one small misstep takes him from the streets of New York City to The Great Before – a fantastical place where new souls get their personalities, quirks and interests before they go to Earth. Determined to return to his life, Joe teams up with a precocious soul, 22 (Tina Fey), who has never understood the appeal of the human experience. As Joe desperately tries to show 22 what’s great about living, he may just discover the answers to some of life’s most important questions.</span></p>\n</blockquote>\n<p data-pw-in-article=\"true\"><em>Soul</em> arrives on Disney+ on <strong>December 25, 2020</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Ood2B6-IY2A:xiIpG1cw9Io:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img
